## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law describes how the reaction rate depends on the concentration of reactants, possibly with time-dependent effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Reaction rate independent of concentration'}
- {'name': 'First-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)'}
- {'name': 'Second-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to square of concentration (bimolecular reaction)'}
- {'name': 'nth-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'General power-law rate dependence on concentration'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order with offset', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Competing first and second order reactions'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order forward reaction with equilibrium (reverse reaction contributing a constant)'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Logistic-type autocatalytic kinetics where product catalyzes the reaction'}
- {'name': 'Substrate inhibition kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2)', 'scenario': 'Enzyme kinetics with substrate inhibition at high concentrations'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent rate (radiation-induced)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Reaction with time-varying external influence (e.g., photolysis with varying light)'}
- {'name': 'Fractional order with time modulation', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * t', 'scenario': 'Power-law kinetics with a time-dependent source or sink term'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive/parallel reaction rate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 + c3', 'scenario': 'Multiple simultaneous reaction pathways consuming or producing A'}
- {'name': 'Saturation kinetics (Michaelis-Menten-like consumption)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1)', 'scenario': 'Enzymatic or catalytic consumption with saturation'}
- {'name': 'Sigmoidal cooperative kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2)', 'scenario': 'Cooperative binding or allosteric enzyme kinetics'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate values (consumption) with concentration dependence → power-law rate law dA_dt = -c * A**n with negative c
- Linear relationship between dA_dt and A → first-order kinetics, look for exponential decay in A(t)
- Quadratic dependence of rate on concentration → bimolecular or dimerization reaction mechanism
- Rate approaching zero as A approaches a nonzero equilibrium → reversible reaction with equilibrium term (c0*A + c1)
- Rate showing a maximum at intermediate A values → autocatalytic mechanism A*(c-A) or substrate inhibition
- Rate independent of time when concentration is controlled → pure concentration-dependent rate law (no explicit t dependence)
- Concave-down relationship between rate and concentration → saturation kinetics or fractional-order kinetics
- Sign change in dA_dt at specific concentration → equilibrium point indicating reversible reaction dynamics
